  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2a3dd493-ad7b-4207-a815-09074b3450a1'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText10541803746954746135" style="display:none">Devastated by the loss of her friend and under constant threat from an unknown spy at Cimmeria Academy, Allie Sheridan is finding it hard to cope.<br /><br />In Fracture, the third book in the Night School series, she’s not the only one losing it – everything is falling apart. And when Nathaniel begins to reveal his game plan, Isabelle starts to lose control.<br /><br />As the school slides into a deadly morass of paranoia and suspicion, everyone is guilty until proved innocent. Anyone can be held without proof, and convicted without a trial. No one is safe.<br /><br />This time Nathaniel doesn’t need to hurt them. This time they’re hurting themselves.</span>

  <u>Genre: YA/Mystery/Romance</u>
</b><br><br>The 3rd book in one of my all time fav series, and guess how it ended up?<br><br>A.DISAPPOINTMENT. <br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380409200ra/801146.gif" alt="141" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/app.php" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409200i/801147.jpg" alt="8db5ee22 50ed 4125 9dee e322c35115ef zpsecc82f7e" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/app.php" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br>When 16 year old Allie Sheridan first arrived at Cimmeria Academy it was as a punishment, to teach her how to be a good respectful student and lady. But now? It's more than that, more than just a school, it's been a safe haven.<br><br><b>But no longer.</b><br><br>A nefarious group - one that is frightingly tied with Allie's family - is trying to destroy everything Cimmeria stands for. <br><br>Even worse, it's clear that somebody they eat with, sleep with, train with...is betraying them. There is a spy in Night school.<br><br><b>As paranoia grows and the fight for Cimmeria begins, it's not an attack from the outside they have to worry about...</b><br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409200i/801148.jpg" alt="f9eeffa7 f0e8 47b7 a5f9 6940a8ff14fa zps78cd9a08" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/app.php" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br>I'm going to keep this review short and straight to the base. <br><br>The Night School series is going downhill, and downhill. The 1st book (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12576579.Night_School__Night_School___1_" title="Night School (Night School, #1) by C.J. Daugherty" rel="nofollow noopener">Night School</a>)was absolutely BRILLIANT! It has 500 pages and i managed to read it in 2 days because i couldn't put it down. The 2nd book (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15757366.Legacy__Night_School___2_" title="Legacy (Night School, #2) by C.J. Daugherty" rel="nofollow noopener">Legacy</a>) was really good too!<br>But <i>Fracture</i> was just....<br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380409200ra/801149.gif" alt="tv addiction emma stone meh gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/app.php" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br><b>I'm actually scared to think of what will become of the next books in the series. </b><br><br>Let's start off with the <b>beginning</b> and why i didn't like it.<br><b>Allie.</b><br>She was back to her old self (being rebellious, doing what she liked, and causing disaster) and she decided to *little spoiler alert* ran away. <br>I understood her reasons and actually approved a bit of her actions. <br>But then she got caught and suddenly she changed her mind about it and she was trying to be the 'good student' again. <br>Why?!<br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380409200ra/801150.gif" alt="bad purpose 2" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/app.php" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br>I found <i>Fracture</i> to be <b>boring</b>. Nothing really happened until the bigger half of the book. The rest was about solving all the mystery and finding out who the traitor was (WHICH WE STILL DON'T KNOW! What is the freaking point of it?)<br><br><b>I wish the book would focus a little more on the romance</b> between Carter, Allie and Sylvain (that's still unsolved too).<br><br><b>Was anything solved at all?...</b><br><br> <a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380409200ra/801151.gif" alt="tumblr m6w0xwe Uh P1qhqb9q" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br><b>
  <u>The ending was;</u>
</b><br><b>Dramatic<br>Ridiculous<br>Stupid</b><br><br>Seriously, <b>the action scenes were very dramatic</b>, i found myself rolling eyes. It was a bit unrealistic too. And stupid because (like i said) nothing was solved. <br><br><b>Overall, sorry but i didn't like it. </b><br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380409200ra/801152.gif" alt="tumblr mqrxrsg8ge1rr0uo4o1 500" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br>At times i couldn't wait to put Fracture down and had to force myself to keep on reading. <br><br><b>Did i finish the book?</b> - <i>Yes</i><br><b>Will i read the next one when it comes out?</b> - <i>Maybe</i><br><b>Am i excited for it? -</b> <i>No</i><br><br><i>Sincerely, The Critic. </i><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><b></b><br><blockquote>
  <b></b>
</blockquote><br><i></i><br><b>
  <u></u>

<div id="review_532851498" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/532851498" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/532851498?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=own-copy">own-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer532851498" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer531180403949367000">4.5 stars <br/><br/>Such a brilliant world! Seriously. C.J. Daugherty's <i>Night School</i> series is one of my favorites books to escape with. I always look forward to the next installment, craving that heart pounding excitement, alluring mystery and charming romance that I've come to expect from these books. I simply adore Daugherty's writing. She is a true master at pacing her stories in a way that plays with your mind and pulls at your heart. The flow and tone is also pitch perfect, but what I love most abou</span>
  <span id="freeText531180403949367000" style="display:none">4.5 stars <br /><br />Such a brilliant world! Seriously. C.J. Daugherty's <i>Night School</i> series is one of my favorites books to escape with. I always look forward to the next installment, craving that heart pounding excitement, alluring mystery and charming romance that I've come to expect from these books. I simply adore Daugherty's writing. She is a true master at pacing her stories in a way that plays with your mind and pulls at your heart. The flow and tone is also pitch perfect, but what I love most about these books is that it's still crazy addicting. I love how unpredictable everything feels, I never know what to expect and I'm continuously guessing from start to finish. I'm happy to say that <b>Fracture</b> is just as riveting and strong as the previous books and once again, an instant favorite!<br /><br />Tormented after the lost of her best friend, Jo, Allie is beside herself. She feels like everyone at Cimmeria Academy has let her down and she doesn't know who she can trust. Wanting to take action into her own hands, Allie escapes the school and tries to find the answers no one else seems to be going after. But her attempt to escape to London failed and Allie is sent back to the Academy. Fueled only by the desperate need to avenge Jo's death, Allie is filled with a new found hope. Revenge. She will train. She will fight and together with her friends, she will find a way to avenge Jo, stop Nathaniel and find the spy lurking in the walls of Cimmeria Academy.<br /><br />I always thought that the third book in a series is the most difficult to write. There is a lot of information and truths that need revealing but you don't want to say to much or give away the entire story. Where's the fun in that? After all, there are two more books planned for this series. So, with that said, Fracture is a great in-between novel, but this was more like a filler then anything else. <br />With the help of their Night School training, Allie and her friends form a secret group and try to plot out who the spy could be. We are treated to seeing these characters fight back in the only way they know how. United. We also finally find out what Night School is truly about and while there were scattered clues among the other books, it was still something else to finally get the grand picture after all this time. I loved how Daugherty waited for the perfect moment to let us in on the big secret, it was a great way for Allie to accept and appreciate where her destiny truly lies as well as capturing that curiosity in readers to keep us guessing and invested. Which totally worked. We learn more about Lucinda's role and how it's connected to Isabelle, Nathaniel and eventually Allie. We also get some action packed scenes that involve Nathaniel and his ultimate goal to take over the school, but at last, we still don't know who the spy is. So, while a lot happens in this installment, at the same time, nothing actually gets resolved. This might be disappointing or frustrating to some readers, but I for one love how Daugherty is setting up for future books. The biggest anchor in these novels has always been the building mystery in both story line and characterizations. When I really think about each of the characters I've grown so attached to, I wonder if I really know them at all. Daugherty has us skeptical of everything about this world. We truly don't' know who we can trust and all we can do is sit back and hope against hope that are favorite characters don't betray us in the end. Yes, the wait can be exasperating, but it also gives us something to ponder and look forward to, which is wonderful since I'm not ready to let these books go just yet. <br /><br />Since the death of Jo, all of these characters seem to grieve and grow in different and even surprising ways.<br />In the begging of the story, Allie is back to her old rebellious ways. She's defiant, hurt and lashes out in mean ways and while she may seem like a brat, she's actually portrayed very realistically. She was the only one there when Jo died. She blames and hates herself and when it doesn't feel big enough, she starts to blame everyone else around her. Later in the book, Allie realizes that she's not the only person who lost a friend that night and that everyone is doing what they can to find the person responsible for helping Jo's killer get inside the school. My heart really goes out to Allie, but I'm glad she finally snapped out of her grief-stricken stage and decided that the best way to avenge Jo was is to fight back. <br />Even Carter and Sylvain decided to put their personal grudge behind them for now and work together, for both Allie and Jo. It was strange to see this unlikely alliance, but it was also really great to see Sylvain and Carter as well as Rachel, Nicole and Zoe work as a team. They have brilliant chemistry and it's exciting and entertaining to see them in action.<br />I'm still waving my Team Carter flag, but I have to admit, Sylvain is growing on me. For someone who I didn't think could be redeemed, Syl turned out to be the only one who is giving the confidence and warmth Allie desperately needs. Carter is acting like his older self that we met in the first book (not really sure who he was in the second) but he still has a lot of issues that he needs to work out.<br />Which brings me to the romance. For now, that part of the story is on hold, but I'm actually glad that Daugherty took this step for Allie. She has so many conflicting problems right now that it would feel forced for her to just pick up where she left off with Slyvain at the Winter ball and her heart still breaks when she thinks of Carter. Allie is confused and lost right now and the last thing she needs to focus on is her love life. So there isn't any romance in this book, but we still got a few heated moments that made my heart smile. <br /><br />All in all, Fracture is another thrilling installment in the Night school series. I'm enjoying the slow but steady rhythm in the plot, the writing is remarkable and these characters are beautifully complicated and compelling. I also really liked the way this ended. It was action packed and gripping and I'm mighty curious where Daugherty will take this next. Another amazing read in the <i>Night School</i> series!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="531180403949367000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_532073924" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/532073924?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer532073924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11348611306176458526"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/>At the beginning of Fracture (which is very appropriately titled, btw), we find Allie utterly broken: angry, defiant, and – underneath it all – impossibly sad. She feels that she can trust no one, not even her headmistress Isabelle, and her grieving heart can’t make peace with everything that happened at the end of Legacy. After a failed escape, Allie returns to Cimmeria with a renewed strength and a taste for revenge. While she still has trust issues, she knows Cimmeria is the only pla</span>
  <span id="freeText11348611306176458526" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br>At the beginning of Fracture (which is very appropriately titled, btw), we find Allie utterly broken: angry, defiant, and – underneath it all – impossibly sad. She feels that she can trust no one, not even her headmistress Isabelle, and her grieving heart can’t make peace with everything that happened at the end of Legacy. After a failed escape, Allie returns to Cimmeria with a renewed strength and a taste for revenge. While she still has trust issues, she knows Cimmeria is the only place where she’s even remotely safe, and she intends to stay alive at all costs. <br><br>With each installment, C.J Daugherty proves herself anew both as a writer and as a master of characterization. Her protagonist is a 16-year-old who is going through things no teen ever should, so some reactions and rash decisions are normal and even expected. I felt that these parts of Allie’s character were done extraordinarily well. Nothing was glossed over, not the anger, not the guilt, and certainly not the rashness of an emotionally immature individual.<br><br>Although present, romance takes a back seat in Fracture as we finally discover what Night School is all about. Carter and Sylvain both play major roles in this installment, but romance is the last thing on anyone’s mind. While I’m usually not one to publicly declare teams, I must make an exception in this case: I am still firmly Team Sylvain. Carter and Allie gave it their best and proved that they’re completely wrong for each other. Carter’s controlling nature rubbed me the wrong way from the beginning, and while Sylvain has made some mistakes in the past, he has certainly atoned for them since.<br><br>Again, the third person narration took some getting used to since I find it more difficult to connect with, but Allie’s pain came through so clearly that I soon stopped noticing it altogether. Regardless of the perspective, Daugherty is a very skilled writer with an excellent sense of pacing. I always thought her books were compulsively readable, but the desperate need to keep turning those pages was stronger than ever with Fracture. <br><br>If you’ve been waiting for answers about Night School and the organization, rest assured, answers you shall get. There were clues before and I had my suspicions, but in Fracture, the purpose of Night School becomes abundantly clear – and scarier than ever. Night School is proving to be a consistently good series – something we sorely lack. I hope it will get even more fans with the US release date so near. <br><br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="11348611306176458526" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1015461614" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7562532885368902431">Fracture begins with an upset Allie, planning to leave Cimmeria. After her failed escape, Allie struggles to come to terms with the events of Legacy, and the fact she still feels, even more so than earlier, that she can't trust anyone at Cimmeria. <br/><br/>The romance in this novel, though subdued, is still there, and I've got to say I definitely preferred Sylvain in this book than the previous books, though Carter is still my favourite of the two. Carter did come across as a bit of a jackass in this boo</span>
  <span id="freeText7562532885368902431" style="display:none">Fracture begins with an upset Allie, planning to leave Cimmeria. After her failed escape, Allie struggles to come to terms with the events of Legacy, and the fact she still feels, even more so than earlier, that she can't trust anyone at Cimmeria. <br /><br />The romance in this novel, though subdued, is still there, and I've got to say I definitely preferred Sylvain in this book than the previous books, though Carter is still my favourite of the two. Carter did come across as a bit of a jackass in this book, which made me definitely dislike him, and I agree that him and Allie definitely appeared not to be a suitable fit here because of that.<br /><br />Allie, who is struggling so much, is the perfect teenage protagonist in this series. She never appears wholly perfect, she makes mistakes, and is emotional - just like any teenage girl would be. <br /><br />Night School plays a major role in this instalment, with more secrets and intrigue coming out, and the action is ramped up even further. Yet again, the ending was dramatic, and full of feels, and I'm so pleased I was able to read book 4 immediately after finishing this.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to everyone, it has quickly become one of my favourite series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7562532885368902431" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7860621906660006242">Okay,Well this book wasn't that exciting compared to the first and second book. it had some perks but there wasn't many. And I am extremely annoyed they haven't yet found out who the spy is in their school. I thought C.J Daugherty would have reviled the spy to us in this book as she didn't revile it in the second. you can't really prolong this bit of the story for long other wise it gets boring as we are waiting to find out who the spy really is so the story doesn't really move on. This what hap</span>
  <span id="freeText7860621906660006242" style="display:none">Okay,Well this book wasn't that exciting compared to the first and second book. it had some perks but there wasn't many. And I am extremely annoyed they haven't yet found out who the spy is in their school. I thought C.J Daugherty would have reviled the spy to us in this book as she didn't revile it in the second. you can't really prolong this bit of the story for long other wise it gets boring as we are waiting to find out who the spy really is so the story doesn't really move on. This what happened in this book, it was on the same page as the last book. As for Allies love interest that didn't move on as well, but I was okay with that as I understood Allie had other things on her mind.<br /><br />I liked the beginning of the book, thought if she didn't get caught by the police the story might have gone much better then it had ended out. the fact that Mark was never mentioned again or played any other part was kind of surprising as Allie had told him certain important things. As to the weird police officers, the book didn't mention anything more about them too.<br /><br />Normally when I am engrossed in a book I read every word, every sentence and every paragraph, and when a book looses my interest I skim through it just to see how the book ends. I found out that half I way I was skimming the book just picking up the important things and glancing over the rest. That kind of shows how I felt about this book.<br /><br />So basically overall the book could have been much more better. Hopefully the next book will have more action and bring the series pace back up<br /></span>

I do think that YA novels can be great and don't really need to follow the typical formula of " we have girl, girl is chosen one, she meets boy, then meets other boy, struggles to chose one". <span id="freeTextContainer8934776731541992288">There were so many small things that bothered me about this book, but in the end I enjoyed it so, so much that I couldn't give it 3 stars. I love the mystery behind every book, how their group of friends act together and apart, the small alliances and closer friendships...the school, loved all of it.<br/><br/>And let's put this here loud and clear, I love Sylvain.   <span id="freeText8934776731541992288" style="display:none">There were so many small things that bothered me about this book, but in the end I enjoyed it so, so much that I couldn't give it 3 stars. I love the mystery behind every book, how their group of friends act together and apart, the small alliances and closer friendships...the school, loved all of it.<br /><br />And let's put this here loud and clear, I love Sylvain. And I'm in this ship for the long ride.<br /><br />What I didn't like was Allie for most of the book, like 80%. She was so annoying, so selfish, so everything. She made stupid decisions all the time, treated Sylvain and Carter like shit, didn't trust her own shadow one moment, and trusted everyone the second. Christ. But after everything I think she will be better in the following books. <br /><br />I think I'll dive into book 4 right away before I leave it hanging on my TBR forever...</span>

<div id="review_688473938" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/688473938" />
    <a title="Allie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19888499-allie"><img alt="Allie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372190082p2/19888499.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/688473938?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allie" href="/user/show/19888499-allie">Allie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19888499-allie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19888499-allie?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer688473938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer960305228832189304"><i>As the paranoia grows and the fights begin, it's not an attack from outside they need to worry about ...</i><br/><br/>What a perfect sentence to describe this book. <br/>After Jo's death Allie and her friends are certain there must be someone on the inside who helped Gabe come in. And it could be everyone - a student, a Night School senior, a guard, a teacher, a friend. Everyone's a suspect. The obsession to find the mole demands all attention and makes Isabelle and Raj blind to what Nathaniel is really planning. </span>
  <span id="freeText960305228832189304" style="display:none"><i>As the paranoia grows and the fights begin, it's not an attack from outside they need to worry about ...</i><br /><br />What a perfect sentence to describe this book. <br />After Jo's death Allie and her friends are certain there must be someone on the inside who helped Gabe come in. And it could be everyone - a student, a Night School senior, a guard, a teacher, a friend. Everyone's a suspect. The obsession to find the mole demands all attention and makes Isabelle and Raj blind to what Nathaniel is really planning. It's up to Allie and her friends to take matters into their own hands. <br /><br />"Fracture" (with the most awesome cover yet :) ) won't let Night School Fans down. The most amazing thing is we finally learn what Cimmeria and Night School really are and why Nathaniel leads a war against Isabelle and Lucinda. I found myself scared the explanation for all of this (killing students? <i>Really?!</i>) might not be good enough and implausible but it wasn't. Yeah, Nathaniels methods are drastic but hey - there's a lot at stake. <br /><br />For whatever reason you are reading the books - the mystery and suspense or the love triangle and romance: You won't be disappointed. Next to grieving about Jo and all the paranoia and actions they have to take to protect Cimmeria and it's students, Allie's still in the middle of her confused feelings for Carter and Sylvain. <br />Personally my little fangirling heart belongs to Allie and Carter but no matter who you ship you'll all get your sweet moments that will make you go all "Awwww" :) <br /><br />The book is leading up to a great finale which will make your heart drop due to the realisation that you have to wait an awfully long time for the next part. How am I gonna survive that?</span>
  <a data-text-id="960305228832189304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth"><img alt="Sarah Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328957304p2/7591340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/713932786?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Elizabeth" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth">Sarah Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-with-abbie">read-with-abbie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=as">as</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer713932786" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9807830319820061943"><b>2.75 stars</b><br/>(Source: I own a copy of this book.)<br/>This is book 3 in the ‘Night School’ series.<br/>Allie is reeling from Jo’s murder, and people seem to be noticing. For Allie, they’re not doing enough to find her murderer though.<br/>Is Gabe still stalking the students? What does he want? And is running away ever the answer?<br/><br/><br/>This was an okay story, but again, Allie was pretty stupid at times, and I got bored.<br/><br/>Allie continued her stupidity in this book, and continued to do whatever she pleased, never once seemi</span>
  <span id="freeText9807830319820061943" style="display:none"><b>2.75 stars</b><br />(Source: I own a copy of this book.)<br />This is book 3 in the ‘Night School’ series.<br />Allie is reeling from Jo’s murder, and people seem to be noticing. For Allie, they’re not doing enough to find her murderer though.<br />Is Gabe still stalking the students? What does he want? And is running away ever the answer?<br /><br /><br />This was an okay story, but again, Allie was pretty stupid at times, and I got bored.<br /><br />Allie continued her stupidity in this book, and continued to do whatever she pleased, never once seeming to worry that she might end up dead. If I’ve said it once, I’ve said it ten times – if you see a suspicious man lurking in the woods, don’t run off after him alone in the dark! It is not a good idea.<br /><br />The storyline in this did become a little unbelievable, even more so than the previous books. Allie’s stupidity continued to be a factor, and some of the things she did were just ridiculous. When there are evil doers lurking around your school, do you go outside gardening alone at 6 am? If someone sees someone suspicious in the old church, do you go running off to see if you can find them?<br />Also some of the things that Allie came out with were ridiculous. I’m sorry, but not wanting to believe a hypothesis because it involves someone having sex with a 40-year-old man, (because that would be gross), is just ridiculous.<br />This book really did bore me in places, and the stuff going on got more and more ridiculous. At the moment I really don’t want to continue with this series at all.<br />Overall; Allie was just stupid, and I got bored.<br />5.5 out of 10.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9807830319820061943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15723377705609708317">Endless idiocy, poor decision-making, and romantic indecision...oh my! (and where the hell are the weapons?)<br/><br/>I enjoyed the first two books, though the heroine could occasionally be annoyingly indecisive. But by book 3 here (Fracture), she had taken this to a whole new level...enough that the book was mostly irritating. Throughout the book, she reverted to the exact same behavior she had grown out of in the very beginning of book 1, made endlessly annoying decisions, and is still completely incapa</span>
  <span id="freeText15723377705609708317" style="display:none">Endless idiocy, poor decision-making, and romantic indecision...oh my! (and where the hell are the weapons?)<br /><br />I enjoyed the first two books, though the heroine could occasionally be annoyingly indecisive. But by book 3 here (Fracture), she had taken this to a whole new level...enough that the book was mostly irritating. Throughout the book, she reverted to the exact same behavior she had grown out of in the very beginning of book 1, made endlessly annoying decisions, and is still completely incapable of making any real choice or understanding anything at all about a relationship. Stop waffling and decide between Carter and Sylvain already. Argh! Seriously girl, learn to tell people your feelings!<br /><br />And another serious bone to pick here - why on earth does NO ONE CARRY A WEAPON?? All sorts of violence happening, attacks, self defense training, ultra security, but not a single gun, and almost no knives...really?<br /><br />*Spoiler alert*<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And where it really got to me - Raj and his 100 security guards decide to follow Allie's plan to rescue Rachel at the castle ruins, but not a one of them brings a sniper rifle to protect Allie while she is playing bait to free Rachel? Not a single gun that can shoot Nathaniel or Gabe? Or shoot down the helicopter? Hell, no one even thinks to shove one or both of them into the tail rotors of the copter? *sigh* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_2292396554" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2292396554" />

<span id="freeTextContainer5736140234507142069">It was a great third book in the Night School-series, which I actually stopped reading months ago after finishing the second book, but I decided to pick it up again and see how it turns out. And let me tell ya-this was a really good choice. I finished it in one sitting, it basically hooked me in from the start and from that moment I could not put it down. I just had to finish it-and this is exactly what I did. So like I said this was a really good book, but compared to the first two books in the</span>
  <span id="freeText5736140234507142069" style="display:none">It was a great third book in the Night School-series, which I actually stopped reading months ago after finishing the second book, but I decided to pick it up again and see how it turns out. And let me tell ya-this was a really good choice. I finished it in one sitting, it basically hooked me in from the start and from that moment I could not put it down. I just had to finish it-and this is exactly what I did. So like I said this was a really good book, but compared to the first two books in the series, I´m not sure if this was the best one. But hey! It was still good.<br>So the story continues with Allie, who in the third book struggles with her ever-changing emotions and the tense situation between the world controlling game. The ending was a little bit disappointing. I was waiting for the grand finale, but sadly it never happened. Some secrets were revealed and we finally got to know every aspect of the main conflict. <br>My overall opinion is 4 stars (:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472923214ra/20358946.gif" width='«200"' height='«90"' alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14077432405510566084">I think this may be the last book in this series that I can stomach. It's just so...BORING! I don't get the appeal of contemporary books and this series in particular doesn't seem to be going anywhere. Well, not anywhere interesting anyway. The whole storyline and reasoning behind the night school is weak at best. A secret society that runs the government in the background? Yawn. It isn't worth all the hype the books try to stir up. I can't take the danger seriously. I mean, why don't they simpl</span>
  <span id="freeText14077432405510566084" style="display:none">I think this may be the last book in this series that I can stomach. It's just so...BORING! I don't get the appeal of contemporary books and this series in particular doesn't seem to be going anywhere. Well, not anywhere interesting anyway. The whole storyline and reasoning behind the night school is weak at best. A secret society that runs the government in the background? Yawn. It isn't worth all the hype the books try to stir up. I can't take the danger seriously. I mean, why don't they simply shoot Nathaniel? It's not rocket science. He doesn't have any super powers, no immortality. Sneak into his operation and shoot him, problem solved.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DOIETVQpe45FtfPcfTTV2hsHtUm05L/apK6T4jEZHdgMRrCFfxKEHAlPA//eE+RkIExYqrWzbef56PHwAKk8Ig==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
